CONTAMINATION THEGDSCC\nOF\nSOIL\nAT\n\nThe Goldstone Deep Space CommunicationsComplex (GDSCC),located in the\nMojave Desert about 40 miles north of Barstow. California.\nand about 160 miles\nnortheast of Pasadena. is part of the National Aeronautics and Space\nAdministration\'s\n(NASA\'s) Deep Space Network (DSN), one of the world\'s larger\nand most sensitive scientific\ntelecommunications\nand\nradio\nnavigation\nnetworks.\nThe\n\nGDSCC\n\nis\n\nPropulsion\nPasadena.\nSection\n\nIII\nThe\n\nSite.\n\nmanaged,\n\nof\n\nfour\n\nsites\n\ndish\nsites\n\nantenna\nat\nthe\n\nbecause\nDSN\n\nis\n\ntwo\n\nbut\n\nDeep\n\nMojave\n\nis\n\nSpace\n\nBase\n\nand\n\noperated\n\nfor\n\nInstitute\nof\nof the\nGDSCC\n\nStation\n\nby\n\nthe\n\nSite.\n\nthat\n\nconsists\n\nAlthough\noperational\n\nsix\nat\n\nwhile\n\nthe\nit\n\nNational\n\nareas\n\nBase\n\n(DSS)\n\nlocated\n\nSite.\n\noperational\n\nMojave\n\nfacilities.\nnow\nare\n\nare\n\noperated\n\ndistinct\n\nSite.\n\nand\nsupport\nGDSCC.\nthere\nantennas\n\nThe\n\nfive\n\nApollo\n\na\n\nand\n\nNASA\n\nby\n\nthe\n\nTechnology\nis presented\n\nJet\n\nin\nin\n\nreport.\n\nincludes\n\nSite.\n\ndirected,\n\n(JPL)\nof the\nCalifornia\nA THEGDSCC\nOF\n\nThe GDSCC located in southern California,\nis\nin a natural, bowl-shaped\ndepression area in the Mojave Desert, in San Bernardino County about 40 miles\nnorth of Barstow, California, and about 160 miles northeast of Pasadena,\nCalifornia, where JPL is located.\nAs indicated in Section I, the GDSCC part of the NASA\'s Deep Space\nis\nNetwork (DSN), one of the world\'s largest and The Echo Station originally\nwas\nbuilt in 1959 as a 26-m (85-ft) antenna. The antenna was first used in 1960 to\nsupport the Echo Project, an experiment to transmit voice communications coastto-coast by bouncing radio signals off the reflective Mylar surface of a passive\nballoon-type satellite.\nIn 1962, this original 26-m antenna was movedto the\nVenus Site.\nIn anticipation of this move, a newer 26-m can\nmaintain\nStanding\nmore\n\nfeatures\nin\n\nis\n\nIn\n\nlatter\n\nbe\n\nseen\n\nfor\nis\n\nthe\n\nlocated\n\nThe Uranus Station Antenna (DSS15) is a 34-m high-efficiency\n(HEF).\nprecision-shaped antenna, located approximately 1,600 ft southeast of the Mars\nStation Antenna. Built in 1984. this antenna at the GDSCC\nfirst was used in\nJanuary 1986 to support the encounter of the Voyager 2 spacecraft with the\nplanet Uranus. The latter is located at a distance of more than 3 billion\nkm\n(1.8 billion miles) from Earth. The new. proposed 34-m, precision-shaped\nantennas, newly constructed at the Venus Site (see above) and planned for the\nApollo Site (see below), are similar in size and structure to this Uranus\nStation antenna.\n4.\n\nApollo Site (DSS 16. DSS17. and DSS24)\n\nThe Apollo Site has a 26-m (85-ft) antenna (DSS16), a 9-m (29.5-ft)\nantenna (DSS17). and 21 buildings, with a combined total area of 43,978 ft 2.\nThe buildings provide space for operations, equipment, storage, and warehousing.\nThe 26-m antenna originally\nwas constructed in 1965 by NASA\'s Goddard Space\nTracking and Data Network to support the mannedApollo missions to the moon.\nOperation of this antenna\nunder\nJPL\nmanagement\nbegan\nin October\n1984.\nBoth\nthe\n26-m\n\nand\n\nthe\n\n9-m\n\nantennas\n\nnow\n\nShuttle\n[Space\nTransportation\nEarth\norbits.\nIn
